## Management Summary

### Verdict

🔴 Juice Shop carries critical security defects across its login, data storage, and server code layers that allow unauthenticated attackers to impersonate any account, read the entire customer database, and execute arbitrary commands on the server. Replacing the authentication design and removing hard-coded credentials are non-negotiable before this application can be safely operated.

**Risk distribution:** 🔴 Critical: 10 · 🟠 High: 42 · 🟡 Medium: 13 · 🟢 Low: 0 · **Total: 65**<br/>**Assessment evidence:** 63 confirmed-exploitable finding(s) · 1 implementation weakness(es) · 7 design weakness(es)


<br/>

**The most damaging attack scenarios include:**

<blockquote style="border-left: 3px solid #dc2626; background: #fef2f2; padding: 16px 20px; margin: 0;">

- **Account takeover without a password** — An attacker can forge a valid login credential by exploiting four independent weaknesses in how the application signs and validates session tokens. *(🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — RSA Private Key Hardcoded as String Literal (`lib/insecurity.ts:21`), 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none, 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Insecure JWT Verification, 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — OAuth Implicit Flow with Algorithmically Derived Password → [W-003](#w-003), [W-007](#w-007))* — ✓ verified attack path
- **Customer records exposed via search** — Unsanitized inputs in the login and product-search flows let an attacker extract every user account and password hash with a single crafted query. *(🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — SQL Injection via String Concatenation in Login Query (`routes/login.ts:34`), 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — SQL injection via unsanitized query parameter in product search (`search.ts:23`) → [W-001](#w-001))*
- **Server takeover via order processing** — An unauthenticated attacker can escape the server-side expression evaluator in the order processing path to run arbitrary operating-system commands. *(🔴 [F-012](#f-012) — Remote code execution via notevil sandbox escape in B2B order endpoint)*
- **Self-promotion to administrator** — Any registered user can grant themselves full administrator access by exploiting how the registration and profile update functions handle role assignments. *(🔴 [F-014](#f-014) — Mass Assignment via finale-rest Auto-CRUD on User Model (`server.ts:501`), 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Mass assignment allows self-registration as admin via role field)*
- **Active sessions stolen via scripts** — Login tokens are stored in browser-accessible memory where any injected script can read them, and there is no server-side way to cancel a stolen session. *(🟠 [F-001](#f-001) — JWT Session Token Written to localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`), 🟠 [F-052](#f-052) — No Server-Side JWT Revocation Mechanism (`lib/insecurity.ts:70`))*

</blockquote>

<br/>

Prioritising the authentication redesign, database query parameterisation, and server-side authorisation checks will close the highest-impact attack paths within a single sprint.

### Top Weaknesses

The systemic root-cause problems behind the findings - the classes to fix, not just individual bugs. Each links to the full [Weakness Register](#7-weakness-register) with its findings and remediation.

- 🔴 **[W-001](#w-001) - Database access relies on concatenated queries** (Critical) - Database queries are assembled from application values instead of passing those values through an enforced parameterised data-access path. _Proven by [F-010](#f-010), [F-011](#f-011)._
- 🔴 **[W-002](#w-002) - Authorization is implemented route by route** (Critical) - Authorization depends on per-handler checks instead of a policy boundary that consistently enforces role, ownership, and tenant scope. _Proven by [F-002](#f-002), [F-013](#f-013), [F-053](#f-053)._
- 🔴 **[W-003](#w-003) - Secrets are committed to source instead of a managed store** (Critical) - Cryptographic keys, credentials, and other high-entropy secrets are embedded as literals in source or config rather than resolved at runtime from a managed secret store, so anyone with repository r… _Proven by [F-004](#f-004), [F-006](#f-006), [F-035](#f-035) (+1 more)._
- 🟠 **[W-004](#w-004) - Endpoints are reachable without enforced authentication** (High) - Sensitive API routes and real-time channels are exposed without an enforced authentication check at the endpoint boundary. _Proven by [F-020](#f-020), [F-054](#f-054)._
- 🟠 **[W-005](#w-005) - Input handling lacks enforced boundary validation** (High) - Request handlers do not validate input against one enforced server-side schema or allowlist at the boundary - validation is either absent on the vulnerable parameters or limited to rejecting select… _Proven by [F-022](#f-022)._
- 🟠 **[W-006](#w-006) - Build pipeline trusts mutable third-party references** (High) - CI/CD workflows resolve third-party actions and other build dependencies to mutable tags or branches instead of immutable commit digests, so a retagged or compromised upstream runs inside the pipel… _Proven by [F-025](#f-025), [F-026](#f-026), [F-038](#f-038) (+2 more)._

### Security Posture & Top Threats

**Figure 1 - Architecture & Top Threats**

Architecture tiers top-to-bottom (External Actors → Client → Application → Data) with the top threats per component. The in-figure legend on the right explains the attack scenarios, severity dots and symbols.

![Figure 1 - Architecture & Top Threats](threat-model-juice-shop-standard-v0.5.figure1.svg)

**Figure 2 - Risk Flow: Actor → Tier → Impact**

Heatmap: **actors** (left) → **architecture tiers** (middle, Client → Application → Data) → **impact** (right). Numbered red arrows ①–⑥ are the threats enumerated in the Top Threats table below.

![Figure 2 - Risk Flow: Actor to Tier to Impact](threat-model-juice-shop-standard-v0.5.figure2.svg)

**Threat actors.** The actors below drive the numbered attack paths in the figures above. The **Shop User** is the *victim* of client-side attacks (XSS / CSRF), not an attacker - in Figure 2 the compromise surfaces as the resulting business-impact node rather than as a separate actor box.

- **Shop User** — legitimate customer; target of client-side attacks; target of ⑤ Output Encoding / Cross-Site Scripting.
- **Anonymous Internet Attacker** — no account; registers in seconds when needed; drives ① Hardcoded Secrets & Weak Cryptography, ② Insecure Query Construction & Data Access, ③ Remote Code Execution (unsafe eval), ⑥ Sensitive File & Secret Exposure.
- **Authenticated Internet Attacker** — owns a regular account; logged in; drives ④ Broken Authorization & Access Control.

**6 structural threats**, grouped by weakness class - each row is one threat, not one finding. *Threat Description* states the general architectural weakness (STRIDE in brackets); *Findings* lists the concrete instances, each linked to [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) with its component; *Risk & Impact* combines severity with business consequence.

|---|------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------|--------|

| <a id="path-injection"></a>② | **Insecure Query Construction & Data Access** _(T·I)_<br/>Database queries in the login and product-search paths are built by concatenating raw user input; a single crafted request can extract the full user table, bypass authentication entirely, or overwrite arbitrary records. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🔴&nbsp;[F-010](#f-010)</span> - SQL Injection via String Concatenation in Login Query (`login.ts:34`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-03](#c-03)</span>&nbsp;Authentication and Authorization Service<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🔴&nbsp;[F-011](#f-011)</span> - SQL injection via unsanitized query parameter in product search (`search.ts:23`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Backend<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-022](#f-022)</span> - Path traversal filesystem access from request input (`dataErasure.ts:104`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Backend<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-024](#f-024)</span> - NoSQL injection allows mass review update via unconstrained _id filter (`updateProductReviews.ts:18`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Backend<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-030](#f-030)</span> - Prompt Injection via Unsanitized User Messages (`chat.ts:191`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-04](#c-04)</span>&nbsp;LLM Chat Service | 🔴 **Critical**<br/>Customer Data Exfiltration · Full Admin Takeover | <span style="white-space:nowrap">● [M-010](#m-010)</span> — Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize parameterised query or ORM finder<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">● [M-011](#m-011)</span> — Parameterize the product search LIKE query |
| <a id="path-remote-code-execution"></a>③ | **Remote Code Execution (unsafe eval)** _(E)_<br/>The B2B order endpoint evaluates user-supplied expressions in a server-side sandbox that can be escaped, granting unauthenticated arbitrary command execution on the host. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🔴&nbsp;[F-012](#f-012)</span> - Remote code execution via `notevil` sandbox escape in B2B order endpoint (`b2bOrder.ts:21`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Backend | 🔴 **Critical**<br/>Full Server Compromise | <span style="white-space:nowrap">● [M-012](#m-012)</span> — Remove server-side expression evaluation from the B2B order endpoint; accept only structured JSON order data |

_STRIDE: S spoofing · T tampering · R repudiation · I information disclosure · D denial of service · E elevation of privilege. Risk, findings, components, impact and Fix are derived deterministically; only the one-line weakness description is authored._

**Verified attack chains.** 2 fully viable ([AC-T-003](#ac-t-003), [AC-T-005](#ac-t-005)); 2 partially blocked ([AC-T-001](#ac-t-001), [AC-T-006](#ac-t-006)). These chains combine individual findings into end-to-end exploitation paths verified step-by-step against the code - see [§9 Abuse Cases](#9-abuse-cases) for the per-step breakdown and blocking mitigations.

### Top Mitigations

Highest-impact P1/P2 mitigations - 21 of 54 qualifying (67 total). Full detail in [§10 Mitigation Register](#10-mitigation-register). All 21 mitigation(s) that fix a Critical finding are always listed here.

| # | Component | Mitigation | Addresses | Effort |
|---|----------------------|------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------|------|
| **1** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ● [M-009](#m-009) — Replace deterministic email-derived password with a cryptographically random credential for OAuth-linked accounts (`oauth.component.ts:30`) | 🔴 [F-009](#f-009) — Derived Credential from OAuth Email Claim (`oauth.component.ts`) | Medium |
| **2** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ● [M-006](#m-006) — Migrate OAuth flow to authorization code + PKCE and decouple OAuth identity from password-based auth (`oauth.component.ts:30`) | 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — OAuth Implicit Flow with Algorithmically Derived Password (`frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts`) | High |
| **3** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-007](#m-007) — Pin JWT algorithm allowlist to RS256 in express-jwt configuration (`insecurity.ts:52`) | 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Insecure JWT Verification (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Low |
| **4** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-011](#m-011) — Parameterize the product search LIKE query (`search.ts:23`) | 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — SQL injection via unsanitized query parameter in product search (`search.ts`) | Low |
| **5** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-014](#m-014) — Add role field to excludeAttributes and enforce role-change authorization in a dedicated admin endpoint (`server.ts:501`) | 🔴 [F-014](#f-014) — Mass Assignment via finale-rest Auto-CRUD on User Model (`server.ts`) | Low |
| **6** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-015](#m-015) — Add role to the finale User resource excludeAttributes list and enforce default role server-side (`server.ts:484`) | 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Mass assignment allows self-registration as admin via role field (`server.ts`) | Low |
| **7** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-012](#m-012) — Remove server-side expression evaluation from the B2B order endpoint; accept only structured JSON order data (`b2bOrder.ts:21`) | 🔴 [F-012](#f-012) — Remote code execution via notevil sandbox escape in B2B order endpoint (`routes/b2bOrder.ts`) | Medium |
| **8** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ● [M-013](#m-013) — Replace `req.body.UserId`/userId/ownerId with `req.user.id` (or equivalent session-derived identity) in every WHERE/filter clause. (`dataExport.ts:26`) | 🔴 [F-013](#f-013) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`routes/dataExport.ts`) | Medium |
| **9** | [C-03](#c-03) — Authentication and Authorization Service | ● [M-005](#m-005) — Pin allowed algorithms to RS256 in expressJwt and `jwt.verify` calls (`insecurity.ts:52`) | 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Low |
| **10** | [C-03](#c-03) — Authentication and Authorization Service | ● [M-010](#m-010) — Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize parameterised query or ORM finder (`login.ts:34`) | 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — SQL Injection via String Concatenation in Login Query (`routes/login.ts`) | Low |
| **11** | [C-03](#c-03) — Authentication and Authorization Service | ● [M-004](#m-004) — Load RSA private key from an environment variable or secret manager at startup (`insecurity.ts:21`) | 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — RSA Private Key Hardcoded as String Literal (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Medium |
| **12** | [C-05](#c-05) — Data Persistence Layer | ● [M-008](#m-008) — Replace MD5 with bcrypt (cost factor ≥12) in User model password setter (`user.ts:76`) | 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Unsalted MD5 Password Hashing (`models/user.ts`) | Medium |
| **13** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ◕ [M-029](#m-029) — Remove bypassSecurityTrustHtml from URL query parameter handling in search-result component (`search-result.component.ts:143`) | 🔴 [F-029](#f-029) — Cross-Site Scripting (`frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts`) | Low |
| **14** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ◕ [M-003](#m-003) — Replace client-side JWT role decode in route guards with server-side authorization check (`app.guard.ts:52`) | 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) — Client-Side-Only Admin and Accounting Role Guard (`frontend/src/app/app.guard.ts`) | Medium |
| **15** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ◕ [M-024](#m-024) — Validate and cast review _id to ObjectID before use in MongoDB query (`updateProductReviews.ts:18`) | 🔴 [F-024](#f-024) — NoSQL injection allows mass review update via unconstrained _id filter (`routes/updateProductReviews.ts`) | Low |
| **16** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ◕ [M-002](#m-002) — Enforce security response headers policy (CSP, HSTS, X-Frame-Options) (`server.ts:370`) | 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Missing Authentication Middleware on Sensitive API Routes (`server.ts`) | Medium |
| **17** | [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend | ◕ [M-035](#m-035) — Replace hardcoded HMAC secret with environment-variable key and add per-answer salt (`insecurity.ts:42`) | 🔴 [F-035](#f-035) — Hardcoded HMAC secret exposes security-answer hashes (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Medium |
| **18** | [C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service | ◕ [M-053](#m-053) — Add server-side discount cap and Zod max constraint to generateCoupon tool input (`chat.ts:179`) | 🔴 [F-053](#f-053) — Discount Cap Unenforced at Server Layer in generateCoupon Tool (`chat.ts`) | Low |
| **19** | [C-07](#c-07) — Real-time WebSocket Channel | ◕ [M-020](#m-020) — Add socket\.io authentication middleware to validate session or JWT on every connection (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`) | 🔴 [F-020](#f-020) — Unauthenticated WebSocket Channel (`lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts`) | Medium |
| **20** | [C-08](#c-08) — Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface | ◕ [M-045](#m-045) — Move Ethereum wallet mnemonic to an environment variable or secrets manager and remove the hardcoded literal (`checkKeys.ts:10`) | 🔴 [F-045](#f-045) — Hardcoded BIP-39 Mnemonic Exposes Ethereum Private Key (`routes/checkKeys.ts`) | Low |
| **21** | [C-08](#c-08) — Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface | ◕ [M-054](#m-054) — Add `security.isAuthorized()` middleware to all web3/NFT route registrations (`checkKeys.ts:7`) | 🔴 [F-054](#f-054) — All Web3/NFT Endpoints Lack Authentication Middleware (`routes/checkKeys.ts`) | Low |

*33 additional P1/P2 mitigations capped from the leader-board · 13 P3 backlog items in [§10 Mitigation Register](#10-mitigation-register). Sorted by priority (P1 first), then component, then leverage (most findings first), severity (Critical first), and effort (Low first).*

### AI / LLM Exposure

The application embeds an LLM-powered chat assistant that processes untrusted user input without sanitization, exposes privileged business functions as tool calls, and transmits user PII to an external provider - creating a direct path from prompt injection to unapproved discount generation. See **[§6 Security Architecture](#6-security-architecture)** for the per-control detail.



- **LLM01 Prompt Injection** — The chat handler concatenates raw user messages directly into the prompt without any sanitization or content policy layer; an attacker can override the system prompt, enumerate tool calls available to the model, and trigger privileged operations such as discount coupon generation. _([C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service)_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-030](#f-030) — Unsanitized user input reaches LLM (`chat.ts:191`)

- **LLM07 System Prompt Leakage** — Prompt injection payloads can extract the confidential system prompt, which encodes business rules and discount constraints that an attacker can then study to craft inputs that reliably exploit tool-call behaviour. _([C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service)_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-043](#f-043) — System prompt leaked via prompt injection (`chat.ts:105`)

- **LLM06 Excessive Agency** — The discount coupon tool enforces no server-side cap; the model can be instructed to issue coupons at any discount percentage, including 100%, because the constraint exists only in the system prompt rather than in server-side business logic. _([C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service)_
  - ↳ 🔴 [F-053](#f-053) — Discount cap absent from server-side tool (`chat.ts:179`)

- **LLM02 Sensitive Information Disclosure** — Full user conversations, including order history and personally identifying messages, are transmitted to an external LLM provider without data minimization or anonymization, creating a third-party data-processing exposure that may conflict with applicable privacy regulations. _([C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service)_
  - ↳ 🟡 [F-062](#f-062) — User PII transmitted to external LLM provider (`chat.ts:203`)

- **LLM10 Unbounded Consumption** — The chat route carries no per-IP or per-user rate limiting and no token budget cap, allowing an unauthenticated caller to exhaust LLM inference quota or drive up operating costs at no marginal cost. _([C-04](#c-04) — LLM Chat Service, [C-02](#c-02) — Express REST API Backend)_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-050](#f-050) — No rate limit or token budget on chat (`server.ts:638`)

### Operational Strengths

Operational controls rated Adequate or Partial - grouped into broad clusters (full per-control breakdown in [§6](#6-security-architecture)). Clusters demoted to Weak by open Critical/High findings appear in [§6](#6-security-architecture) instead, not here.

<table style="table-layout:fixed;width:100%">
<colgroup><col width="20%" style="width:20%"><col width="33%" style="width:33%"><col width="47%" style="width:47%"></colgroup>
<thead><tr><th>Strength</th><th>What's in Place</th><th>Effectiveness</th></tr></thead>
<tbody>
<tr><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere"><strong>Container &amp; Supply-Chain Hardening</strong></td><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere"><em>Build-time and runtime hardening - minimal base image, non-root execution, dependency inventory.</em><br/>Automated SCA scanning<br/>Container Security</td><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere">✅ Adequate</td></tr>
<tr><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere"><strong>Hardened HTTP Stack</strong></td><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere"><em>Browser-facing HTTP hardening - security headers, cookie flags, cross-origin policy, and abuse-protection limits.</em><br/>HSTS and Security Headers<br/>CORS Configuration</td><td style="overflow-wrap:anywhere">⚠️ Partial - Bypassed by 1 High finding(s) of the kind this cluster is supposed to prevent - e.g.<br/>🟠 <a href="#f-036">F-036</a> — SSRF via unconstrained profile image URL fetch (<code>profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24</code>).</td></tr>
</tbody>
</table>


**Bottom line:** These controls narrow specific attack surfaces but none eliminates a Critical finding on its own.

<a id="critical-attack-chain"></a><a id="critical-attack-tree"></a>
## Critical Attack Tree

The root is the worst-case attacker goal; below it, each capability branch groups the Critical findings that achieve it. Branches feed the goal by OR - any single path suffices.

```mermaid
graph LR
    G_ROOT["Full admin takeover and data exfiltration"]:::goal
    OR_AUTH["Forge or steal admin session"]:::or_node
    L_T004["F-004 - Hardcoded RSA signing key"]:::leaf
    L_T005["F-005 - Algorithm-none accepted"]:::leaf
    L_T007["F-007 - Insecure token verification"]:::leaf
    L_T006["F-006 - Derived OAuth password"]:::leaf
    L_T008["F-008 - Weak password hash"]:::leaf
    L_T009["F-009 - Email-derived credential"]:::leaf
    OR_INJECT["Inject into data layer"]:::or_node
    L_T010["F-010 - Login SQL injection"]:::leaf
    L_T011["F-011 - Search SQL injection"]:::leaf
    OR_EOP["Escalate privilege or execute code"]:::or_node
    L_T012["F-012 - RCE sandbox escape"]:::leaf
    L_T013["F-013 - Direct object reference bypass"]:::leaf
    L_T014["F-014 - Mass assignment auto-CRUD"]:::leaf
    L_T015["F-015 - Mass assignment admin role"]:::leaf

    OR_AUTH -->|"OR"| G_ROOT
    L_T004 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T005 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T007 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T006 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T008 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T009 -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    OR_INJECT -->|"OR"| G_ROOT
    L_T010 -->|"OR"| OR_INJECT
    L_T011 -->|"OR"| OR_INJECT
    OR_EOP -->|"OR"| G_ROOT
    L_T012 -->|"OR"| OR_EOP
    L_T013 -->|"OR"| OR_EOP
    L_T014 -->|"OR"| OR_EOP
    L_T015 -->|"OR"| OR_EOP

    classDef goal fill:#0f172a,stroke:#000,color:#fff,stroke-width:3px
    classDef and_node fill:#334155,stroke:#1e293b,color:#fff,stroke-width:2px
    classDef or_node fill:#64748b,stroke:#334155,color:#fff,stroke-width:2px
    classDef leaf fill:#f3dada,stroke:#b71c1c,color:#7f0000,stroke-width:2px
```

**Findings** (full detail in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register)): [F-004](#f-004) · [F-005](#f-005) · [F-007](#f-007) · [F-006](#f-006) · [F-008](#f-008) · [F-009](#f-009) · [F-010](#f-010) · [F-011](#f-011) · [F-012](#f-012) · [F-013](#f-013) · [F-014](#f-014) · [F-015](#f-015)

---

## 1. System Overview

Probably the most modern and sophisticated insecure web application

**Repository:** https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop.git
**Runtime:** Node\.js 22 - 26

### Scope

This threat model covers 8 components of juice-shop: **Angular SPA Frontend**, **Express REST API Backend**, **Authentication and Authorization Service**, **LLM Chat Service**, **Data Persistence Layer**, **CI/CD Pipeline**, **Real-time WebSocket Channel**, **Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface**.

All 8 modeled components received full STRIDE threat analysis.

**Out of scope:** third-party hosted dependencies, browser runtime, operating-system kernel, and the underlying network infrastructure.

---

## 2. Architecture Diagrams

### 2.1 System Context

Who interacts with juice-shop from the outside, and through which channels. Solid arrows show normal usage; dashed red arrows mark unauthenticated probing or exploit paths (C4 Level 1).

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    USER["End User<br/>(browser)"]
    ATTACKER["Anonymous<br/>Internet Attacker"]
    ADMIN["Admin User"]
    SYSTEM["juice-shop"]
    EXTERNAL["External HTTP Services<br/>(SSRF target)"]
    USER -->|HTTPS · normal usage| SYSTEM
    ATTACKER -.->|HTTPS · probing / exploit| SYSTEM
    ADMIN -->|HTTPS · admin actions| SYSTEM
    SYSTEM -->|outbound · HTTPS| EXTERNAL
    classDef user     fill:#e8f1ea,stroke:#2e7d32,color:#1b5e20,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef attacker fill:#f3dada,stroke:#b71c1c,color:#7f0000,stroke-width:2px
    classDef admin    fill:#fef3c7,stroke:#b45309,color:#78350f,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef sys      fill:#f2f2f2,stroke:#424242,color:#111,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef ext      fill:#f2f2f2,stroke:#9e9e9e,color:#424242,stroke-dasharray:3 3,stroke-width:1px
    class USER user
    class ATTACKER attacker
    class ADMIN admin
    class SYSTEM sys
    class EXTERNAL ext
```

**Key takeaway:** Every actor in the context interacts with juice-shop through its external interface, so authentication and input validation at that edge govern the entire attack surface.

### 2.2 Container Architecture

How the system decomposes into deployable units. Each box is a separate runtime process or service container; arrows show synchronous request paths between them. Components with ≥3 Critical findings carry a red border, ≥2 High amber (C4 Level 2).

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph Client
        frontend_spa["Angular SPA Frontend"]
        auth_service["Authentication and Authorization Service"]
    end
    subgraph Application
        backend_api["Express REST API Backend"]
        llm_chat_service["LLM Chat Service"]
        ci_cd_pipeline["CI/CD Pipeline"]
        realtime_channel["Real-time WebSocket Channel"]
        web3_nft["Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface"]
    end
    subgraph Data
        data_persistence[("Data Persistence Layer")]
    end
    frontend_spa -->|HTTPS REST| backend_api
    auth_service -->|HTTPS REST| backend_api
    backend_api -->|driver| data_persistence
    backend_api -->|in-process| llm_chat_service
    backend_api -->|in-process| ci_cd_pipeline
    backend_api -->|in-process| realtime_channel
    backend_api -->|in-process| web3_nft
    classDef critical fill:#f3dada,stroke:#b71c1c,color:#7f0000,stroke-width:3px
    classDef warning  fill:#fef3c7,stroke:#b45309,color:#78350f,stroke-width:2px
    class backend_api critical
    class auth_service critical
    class frontend_spa warning
    class llm_chat_service warning
    class data_persistence warning
    class ci_cd_pipeline warning
    class realtime_channel warning
    class web3_nft warning
```

**Key takeaway:** The system decomposes into 2 client, 5 application and 1 data unit(s); Express REST API Backend carries the most Critical findings (6) and bounds the worst-case blast radius.

Who reaches each component, and through which trust zone. The technology stack the system is built on. Each box names the framework or runtime that fills that role; per-component findings live in the [§2.3](#23-components) component table above, and the full per-finding catalogue is in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register).

## 3. Attack Walkthroughs

This section walks through how the highest-risk findings are exploited. To keep the section focused, it covers the **8 highest-priority of 12 Critical findings** (chain entry points and the findings closest to a breach); every remaining Critical still has a full [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) row with the same evidence, impact, and fix. Each walkthrough has attack steps, a focused sequence diagram, and the primary mitigation. The cross-finding view (which weaknesses combine toward the worst-case goal, and where one fix severs several paths) is in the [Critical Attack Tree](#critical-attack-tree). Full per-finding context - severity rationale, assets, detection signals - is in the [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) row for each finding.

### 3.1 Insecure JWT Verification in Express REST API Backend

**Source:** 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — `lib/insecurity.ts:52`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-007](#f-007) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The `isAuthorized()` middleware is configured as `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` without specifying an `algorithms` allowlist.
2. The public key is exposed at `/encryptionkeys/jwt.pub` (unauthenticated directory listing).
3. An attacker downloads the public key, crafts a JWT with header `{ alg: 'HS256' }`, signs it with the public key bytes used as the HMAC-SHA256 secret, and submits it.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: backend-api - lib/insecurity.ts:52
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting lib/insecurity.ts line 52
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-347
    alt Current state — F-007
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-007
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-007 — Pin JWT algorithm allowlist to RS256 in express-jwt configur
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-007](#m-007) (Pin JWT algorithm allowlist to `RS256` in express-jwt configur) lands, 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Insecure JWT Verification is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:52` (Critical-severity, [CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-007](#m-007) (Pin JWT algorithm allowlist to `RS256` in express-jwt configuration)

### 3.2 Unsalted MD5 Password Hashing in User

**Source:** 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — `models/user.ts:76`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-008](#f-008) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The User model's password setter at `models/user.ts:76` calls `security.hash(clearTextPassword)`, which resolves to `crypto.createHash('md5').update(data).digest('hex')` (`lib/insecurity.ts:41`).
2. `MD5` is a broken hash function: it produces a 128-bit digest with no per-user salt, completing in nanoseconds on modern GPUs.
3. An attacker who obtains the Users table - via the SQL injection at `routes/search.ts:23`, a backup leak, or direct SQLite file access - can crack all password hashes offline using precomputed rainbow tables or GPU-accelerated brute force.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: data-persistence - models/user.ts:76
    Attacker->>Attacker: Craft JWT with header alg=none and admin claims
    Attacker->>App: Crafted HTTP request to the affected endpoint with the unsigned token in Authorization
    App->>App: Validate token without pinning the signing algorithm
    App-->>Attacker: 200 OK - request authorised under forged admin identity
    alt Current state — F-008
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-008
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-008 — Replace MD5 with bcrypt (cost factor ≥12) in User model pass
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-008](#m-008) (Replace `MD5` with bcrypt (cost factor ≥12) in User model pass) lands, 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Unsalted MD5 Password Hashing (`models/user.ts:76`) is exploitable at `models/user.ts:76` (Critical-severity, [CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-008](#m-008) (Replace `MD5` with bcrypt (cost factor ≥12) in User model password setter)

### 3.3 SQL Injection in Authentication and Authorization Service

**Source:** 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — `routes/login.ts:34`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-010](#f-010) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The login handler at `routes/login.ts:34` builds its SQL query by direct string interpolation: `SELECT * FROM Users WHERE email = '${req.body.email || ''}' AND password = '${security.hash(req.body.password || '')}'`.
2. An attacker submits `email = \' OR 1=1 --` to collapse the WHERE clause, logging in as the first user in the table (typically the administrator).
3. More destructively, UNION-based injection (`' UNION SELECT * FROM Users --`) exfiltrates the full user table including password hashes.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant DB
    Note over API: auth-service - routes/login.ts:34
    Note over DB: Database
    Attacker->>API: Reflected attacker-controlled input (HTML payload) with classical OR 1=1 payload
    API->>DB: SQL built by string interpolation - payload becomes query
    DB-->>API: First matching row regardless of intended predicate
    API-->>Attacker: 200 OK with authenticated session / leaked rows
    alt Current state — F-010
        Attacker->>API: The attacker sends the exploit for F-010
        API-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-010 — Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize paramete
        Attacker->>API: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-010](#m-010) (Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize paramete) lands, 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — SQL Injection via String Concatenation in Login Query (`routes/login.ts:34`) is exploitable at `routes/login.ts:34` (Critical-severity, [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-010](#m-010) (Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize parameterised query or ORM finder)

### 3.4 SQL injection in Express REST API Backend

**Source:** 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — `routes/search.ts:23`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-011](#f-011) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The product search handler interpolates `req.query.q` directly into a LIKE clause: `SELECT * FROM Products WHERE ((name LIKE '%${criteria}%' OR description LIKE '%${criteria}%') AND deletedAt IS NULL)`.
2. Submitting `q=')) UNION SELECT sql,2,3,4,5,6,7,8,9 FROM sqlite_master--` dumps the entire database schema.
3. The 200-character truncation does not prevent exploitation - a union injection payload fits in 200 characters.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant DB
    Note over API: backend-api - routes/search.ts:23
    Note over DB: Database
    Attacker->>API: Crafted search query (HTML payload in `q=` parameter) with classical OR 1=1 payload
    API->>DB: SQL built by string interpolation - payload becomes query
    DB-->>API: First matching row regardless of intended predicate
    API-->>Attacker: 200 OK with authenticated session / leaked rows
    alt Current state — F-011
        Attacker->>API: The attacker sends the exploit for F-011
        API-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-011 — Parameterize the product search LIKE query
        Attacker->>API: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-011](#m-011) (Parameterize the product search LIKE query) lands, 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — SQL injection via unsanitized query parameter in product search (`search.ts:23`) is exploitable at `routes/search.ts:23` (Critical-severity, [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-011](#m-011) (Parameterize the product search LIKE query)

### 3.5 Mass Assignment in Express REST API Backend

**Source:** 🔴 [F-014](#f-014) — `server.ts:501`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-014](#f-014) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. Juice Shop registers all Sequelize models as finale-rest resources at `server.ts:481-507`.
2. For the User model (line 484), only `password` and `totpSecret` are in the `excludeAttributes` list - the `role` field is fully writable via API.
3. A PUT or PATCH to `/api/Users/:id` with body `{"role": "admin"}` will persist the admin role directly to the Users table without any privilege check.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: backend-api - server.ts:501
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting server.ts line 501
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-915
    alt Current state — F-014
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-014
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-014 — Add role field to excludeAttributes and enforce role-change
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-014](#m-014) (Add role field to excludeAttributes and enforce role-change ) lands, 🔴 [F-014](#f-014) — Mass Assignment via finale-rest Auto-CRUD on User Model (`server.ts:501`) is exploitable at `server.ts:501` (Critical-severity, [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-014](#m-014) (Add role field to excludeAttributes and enforce role-change authorization in a dedicated admin endpoint)

### 3.6 Mass assignment allows self-registration as admin in Express REST API Backend

**Source:** 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — `server.ts:484`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)). STRIDE: Elevation of Privilege. See [§8 F-015](#f-015) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The `finale.resource` auto-generated endpoint for the User model at `server.ts:483-498` excludes only `password` and `totpSecret` from the create operation.
2. The `role` field (values: `customer`, `deluxe`, `accounting`, `admin`) is not in the `exclude` list.
3. Any unauthenticated attacker can `POST /api/Users { "email": "evil@evil.com", "password": "pass", "role": "admin" }` and receive a new account with `role: 'admin'`.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: backend-api - server.ts:484
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting server.ts line 484
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-915
    alt Current state — F-015
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-015
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-015 — Add role to the finale User resource excludeAttributes list
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-015](#m-015) (Add role to the finale User resource excludeAttributes list ) lands, 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Mass assignment allows self-registration as admin via role field is exploitable at `server.ts:484` (Critical-severity, [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-015](#m-015) (Add role to the finale User resource excludeAttributes list and enforce default role server-side)

### 3.7 JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none

**Source:** 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — `lib/insecurity.ts:52`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-327](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/327.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-005](#f-005) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. express-jwt 0.1.3 is configured at `lib/insecurity.ts:52` as `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` with no `algorithms` allowlist.
2. The jsonwebtoken 0.4.0 library (`package.json:132`) honours the algorithm field embedded in the JWT header, including the `alg:none` special value that disables signature verification entirely.
3. An unauthenticated attacker crafts a JWT with header `{"alg":"none"}`, omits the signature, and places any valid-looking user payload (including `{"data":{"role":"admin"}}`) in the body.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: auth-service - lib/insecurity.ts:52
    Attacker->>App: GET /jwks or read RSA public key from the repo
    App-->>Attacker: Public RSA key (intended for RS256 verification)
    Attacker->>Attacker: Sign forged JWT with HS256 using the RSA public key as the HMAC secret (or set alg=none and drop the signature)
    Attacker->>App: Authenticated request carrying the forged token
    App-->>Attacker: 200 OK - server accepts the forged token because it does not enforce algorithm binding
    alt Current state — F-005
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-005
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-005 — Pin allowed algorithms to RS256 in expressJwt and jwt.verify
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-005](#m-005) (Pin allowed algorithms to `RS256` in expressJwt and `jwt.verify`) lands, 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:52` (Critical-severity, [CWE-327](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/327.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-005](#m-005) (Pin allowed algorithms to `RS256` in expressJwt and `jwt.verify` calls)

### 3.8 RSA Private Key Hardcoded as String Literal

**Source:** 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — `lib/insecurity.ts:21`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-004](#f-004) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The 1024-bit RSA private key used to sign all JWTs is embedded verbatim as a multi-line string constant at `lib/insecurity.ts:21`.
2. Any developer, contractor, or attacker with read access to the source repository (GitHub, CI artefacts, compiled bundles) possesses the signing key.
3. With it, they can mint arbitrary JWTs that pass `jwt.verify` at line 189 and every `isAuthorized()` middleware check - bypassing authentication for all protected endpoints.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant Repo
    participant App
    Note over Repo: Public repository
    Note over App: auth-service - lib/insecurity.ts:21
    Attacker->>Repo: Clone or browse - extract private key from lib/insecurity.ts line 21
    Attacker->>Attacker: Sign forged token / signature with the extracted key
    Attacker->>App: Submit forged artefact in normal authentication flow
    App-->>Attacker: Request accepted as authentic - signature validates
    alt Current state — F-004
        Attacker->>Repo: The attacker sends the exploit for F-004
        Repo-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-004 — Load RSA private key from an environment variable or secret
        Attacker->>Repo: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        Repo-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-004](#m-004) (Load RSA private key from an environment variable or secret ) lands, 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — RSA Private Key Hardcoded as String Literal (`lib/insecurity.ts:21`) is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` (Critical-severity, [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-004](#m-004) (Load RSA private key from an environment variable or secret manager at startup)

## 4. Assets

Information assets and the classification level that drives the Confidentiality / Integrity / Availability targets used in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) risk scoring.

| Asset | Classification | Description |
|----------------------|--------------|------------------------------------|
| User Credentials (Passwords + JWT Tokens) | Restricted | Bcrypt-hashed passwords in database;<br/>plaintext passwords in transit during login;<br/>JWT tokens in browser localStorage and HTTP<br/>headers. Compromise yields account takeover<br/>for all users. |
| LLM System Prompt and API Keys | Restricted | Chatbot system prompt containing business<br/>instructions and intended-to-be-secret rules<br/>(intentional extraction challenge). LLM API<br/>key (`OPENAI_API_KEY_OVERRIDE`) in<br/>environment. Exposure enables prompt<br/>injection and LLM provider billing abuse. |
| JWT Signing Key | Restricted | HMAC-SHA256 symmetric signing key used by<br/>jsonwebtoken 0.4.0 to issue JWTs. Stored in<br/>server-side configuration<br/>(`lib/insecurity.ts`). Compromise enables<br/>forgery of any user or admin session token. |
| OAuth2 Client Secrets (Google, GitHub) | Restricted | OAuth2 client IDs and secrets for Google and<br/>GitHub social login Passport strategies.<br/>Stored in environment variables or<br/>configuration. Exposure enables social login<br/>impersonation. |
| CI/CD Pipeline Secrets (`BOT_TOKEN`,<br/>`GITHUB_TOKEN`) | Restricted | GitHub Actions secrets: `BOT_TOKEN`<br/>(repository write access for automated PRs),<br/>`GITHUB_TOKEN` (workflow permissions).<br/>Compromise enables repository manipulation<br/>or malicious build artifact injection. |
| User PII (Email, Name, Delivery Address) | Confidential | User email addresses, full names, delivery<br/>addresses, and profile data stored in<br/>Sequelize database. Used for GDPR/privacy<br/>regulation scope. |
| Payment and Order Data | Confidential | Credit card details (intentionally<br/>vulnerable for demo), order history, basket<br/>contents, wallet balances. Stored in<br/>database. Real PCI-DSS data handling scope<br/>in non-training context. |
| Database (SQLite File / PostgreSQL Instance) | Confidential | Primary data store containing all<br/>application data: users, orders, products,<br/>feedback, chat logs. SQLite default means<br/>single-file database on filesystem.<br/>Sequelize ORM layer with intentional SQLi<br/>challenge bypass paths. |
| LLM Chat Conversation History | Confidential | User conversational data sent to external<br/>LLM provider. May contain PII, order<br/>details, or sensitive queries. Governed by<br/>provider's data retention policy. Privacy<br/>risk when using cloud-hosted LLM providers. |
| Uploaded User Files (Profile Images,<br/>Complaints) | Internal | User-uploaded files stored in ftp/<br/>directory. Includes profile pictures and<br/>complaint attachments. Path traversal and<br/>malicious file upload vectors apply<br/>(intentional challenge targets). |
| Application Source Code and Challenges<br/>Configuration | Internal | Full application source code (public GitHub<br/>repo). Challenge definitions in<br/>`data/static/challenges.yml` reveal all<br/>intended vulnerability locations. Public<br/>repo means attacker recon is unrestricted. |
| Prometheus Metrics | Internal | Runtime metrics at `/metrics` endpoint<br/>(request counts, response times, Node\.js<br/>heap). Unauthenticated in baseline<br/>configuration. Leaks application behavior<br/>patterns and error distribution. |

## 5. Attack Surface

Network-reachable entry points classified by authentication requirement. Each row links to the threat(s) referenced in its **Notes** column. The **Risk** column reflects the highest-severity linked finding. Entry points with no linked finding are still listed when they sit on a sensitive surface (authentication, registration, management) or look like a missing-auth/authz suspect - marked **⚑ Review** in Notes.
